### Task Description:
You are to write a Python function that analyzes a list of patients' ages and determines the percentage of patients who fall into specific age categories: infants (0-1 years), toddlers (2-4 years), children (5-12 years), and teenagers (13-18 years). The input will be a list of integers representing the ages of patients. The output should be a dictionary where the keys are the age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and the values are the percentage of total patients that fall into each category, rounded to two decimal places.

### Specific Requirements:
1. The function must be named `analyze_patient_ages` and take a single parameter `ages`, which is a list of integers.
2. The output must be a dictionary with the exact keys: 'infants', 'toddlers', 'children', and 'teenagers'.
3. The percentages must be rounded to two decimal places.

6. The explanation must clearly describe the function's logic, including how the age categories are determined and how the percentages are calculated.
7. The final output should be formatted as a Python dictionary, and the explanation should be written in natural, clear English without markdown formatting.
8. Responses and only responses should be separated by 6 asterisk symbols: ****** if multiple responses are required.
9. Enclose any individual word or phrase in square brackets if specified in the input.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Categorize each age into one of the four predefined ranges.
- Count the number of patients in each category.
- Calculate the percentage of patients in each category relative to the total number of patients.
- Round the percentages to two decimal places.
- Ensure the output format matches the specified structure.
- Follow the exact formatting and positioning instructions for the keyword "reach" and excluded keywords.

For the elective course problem, the task involves calculating the number of ways students can choose 3 courses from 10, with the constraint that courses A, B, and C cannot all be selected together. This requires considering two scenarios: one where none of A, B, or C are selected, and another where exactly one of them is selected. The total number of combinations is the sum of these two scenarios.  

***  

Courses A, B, C are mutually exclusive. Other courses are freely selectable.  
Students must choose 3 courses total. No more than one of A, B, or C can be chosen.  

***  

Students can select 3 courses from the 7 non-conflicting ones. They can also choose 1 from A, B, or C.  
This leads to two distinct combinations: 7 choose 3 and 3 choose 1.  

***  

The total number of combinations is the sum of the two scenarios. The final answer is 35 plus 3.  
Answer is 38.

You are given a task that involves both mathematical modeling and optimization, with specific formatting and content constraints. The task is to develop a mathematical model for optimizing the layout of UI components in a graph, considering both rendering time and user interaction latency. The model must account for device-specific constants, component sizes, resolutions, and dependency depths. Additionally, the response must include the word "mirror" exactly 5 times and end each sentence with the word "chemical" before punctuation. No commas should be used in the entire response.

The layout of UI components is represented as a graph $ G = (V, E) $, where each vertex $ v \in V $ represents a UI component and each edge $ e \in E $ represents a dependency between components. The rendering time for a component $ v_i $ is a function $ R(v_i) = \alpha_i \cdot f(s_i, r_i) $, where $ \alpha_i $ is a device-specific constant, $ s_i $ is the size of the component, and $ r_i $ is the resolution of the component. The goal is to minimize the total rendering time across all components for both desktop and mobile device profiles.

The model must also include a constraint on user interaction latency, which should not exceed a threshold $ L $ seconds. The latency $ L(v_i) $ for each component $ v_i $ is a function of the depth of $ v_i $ in the dependency graph and is given by $ L(v_i) = \beta_i \cdot g(d_i) $, where $ \beta_i $ is a device-specific constant and $ d_i $ is the depth of the component in the graph. The optimization problem must simultaneously minimize the total rendering time and satisfy the latency constraint for every component in the graph.

Ensure that the word "mirror" appears exactly 5 times and that the last word of each sentence, before punctuation, is the word "chemical". Refrain from using any commas in your response. Your answer should be concise and precise, addressing the mathematical formulation of the problem and the optimization criteria.

2. **Task Description**: Determine the exact task the assistant is expected to perform.
3. **Constraints**: List all the constraints mentioned in the examples, including any formatting, content, or structural requirements.
4. **Niche and Domain-Specific Information**: Extract any domain-specific knowledge or facts that are crucial to solving the task.
5. **Generalizable Strategy**: Identify any generalizable approach or method that the assistant used to solve the task, which can be applied to future similar tasks.

## Example Analysis

### Example 1
- **Input Format**: A mathematical problem with two parts, including a polynomial function and an inequality.
- **Task Description**: Solve a calculus problem to find the maximum of a polynomial function and solve an inequality with a constraint.
- **Constraints**:
  - Include a specific keyword in a specific position of the first sentence.
  - Provide a complete response that meets all requirements.
- **Niche and Domain-Specific Information**:
  - Use of calculus (derivatives, critical points, second derivative test).
  - Optimization under a constraint.
- **Generalizable Strategy**:
  - Differentiate the function to find critical points.
  - Use the second derivative test to determine maxima/minima.
  - Solve inequalities with constraints.

### Example 2
- **Input Format**: A Python programming task with a specific function to write.
- **Task Description**: Write a Python function to extract and count unique email domains from a list of email addresses.
- **Constraints**:
  - Highlight at least two sections in markdown.
  - Provide a function with a clear docstring and explanation.
  - Ensure the output is an integer.
- **Niche and Domain-Specific Information**:
  - Email address parsing.
  - Set data structure for uniqueness.
  - Marketing analytics in digital advertising.
- **Generalizable Strategy**:
  - Use string manipulation to extract the domain.
  - Store unique domains in a set.
  - Return the length of the set as the count.

### Example 3
- **Input Format**: A word problem involving percentages and fractions.
- **Task Description**: Calculate the number of books Maria will recommend based on her reading habits.
- **Constraints**:
  - Exclude specific keywords.
  - Ensure the final answer is a whole number.
- **Niche and Domain-Specific Information**:
  - Percentage increase calculation.
  - Fractional recommendation rate.
- **Generalizable Strategy**:
  - Calculate the new number of books read using percentage increase.
  - Apply the recommendation rate to determine the number of books to recommend.
  - Round the result to the nearest whole number if necessary.
